<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_0b851ad7-1f1c-47cd-bb73-df12b740e00e'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

<div id="review_111492527" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/111492527" />
    <a title="Slavena" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3633862-slavena"><img alt="Slavena" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1407501224p2/3633862.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/111492527?book_show_action=true">Jul 13, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Slavena" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Slavena" href="/user/show/3633862-slavena">Slavena</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3633862-slavena?shelf=contemporary-romance">contemporary-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3633862-slavena?shelf=best-romance-books">best-romance-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer111492527" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer214129484554390382">I really enjoyed this one. I know that Paradise rates so much higher and is considered best of Judith McNaught contemporary romance but I have to disagree. I liked this one better. May be its because there wasn’t so much “work” talk since this contemporary romance is old, no cell phones, people are using typewriters and women are wearing bolero, which is a clothing item most young people may not even recognize. <br/><br/>Nick Sinclair is a modern rake, successful, very sexy and with a trail of admiring wo</span>
  <span id="freeText214129484554390382" style="display:none">I really enjoyed this one. I know that Paradise rates so much higher and is considered best of Judith McNaught contemporary romance but I have to disagree. I liked this one better. May be its because there wasn’t so much “work” talk since this contemporary romance is old, no cell phones, people are using typewriters and women are wearing bolero, which is a clothing item most young people may not even recognize. <br /><br />Nick Sinclair is a modern rake, successful, very sexy and with a trail of admiring women. I liked Nick but he is not a typical McNaught character where he meets heroine and pursues her right away. No, he wants to have some fun but nothing beyond that. For the first part of the book we draw conclusions only from dialogue, McNaught never writes from his point of view or describes his feelings, which is what she does in all other books I have read.<br /><br />Lauren is beautiful, charming, witty and adorable. I read reviews where people did not like her but I did like her a lot. In my world her reaction to a beautiful guy who pays her attention is very realistic, she thinks she loves him from the start and I have to tell you I have felt like that as well so I don’t think her being smitten, moreover when she hasn’t met many guys is surprising. When she realizes that Nick is just having fun with her and had no intention of a real relationship she grows fast and this is when the book gets fun. Nick and Lauren’s witty dialogue and their meetings at work were fantastic. I laughed and I was saying to her “You go girl”. I like it when heroines stir jealousy in the hero and prove him he is not all that. She turned into my favorite character – spitfire hellcat:)<br /><br />Also this book is not like your usual McNaught, I finished it in 5hrs, its not so large in volume as the rest but for me it was a good book, I would not compare it to her historicals because I think those will always be her best works but this book deserves attention too.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="214129484554390382" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText16192211999726055663" style="display:none">This is my first <strong>Judith McNaught</strong> book and though I have a problem with the story there's no denying that the author knows how to weave her words and pull a reader's attention. There's just no excuse unless it's use for pleasure. Can't a woman explain herself first? Can't she at least deserved that?<br /><br />I would have rated this higher if I find justice for the ending but no can do.</span>

<div id="review_125252854" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/125252854" />
    <a title="Amy Sanders" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3550768-amy-sanders"><img alt="Amy Sanders" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1306357881p2/3550768.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/125252854?book_show_action=true">Oct 07, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amy Sanders" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amy Sanders" href="/user/show/3550768-amy-sanders">Amy Sanders</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer125252854" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9459372006927775249">Another reviewer pointed out that this was definitely an 80's book, as an employer who treated an employee this way would have made the girl very wealthy. <br/>His treatment of her from the beginning was terrible. She was very naive. I was glad to see that she stood up to him for the majority of the book. There were some of her comments that I wanted to stand up and cheer. <br/><br/>The end was too abrupt. I know this is JM's earlier writing, but I know that some of her newer offerings don't always give enough</span>
  <span id="freeText9459372006927775249" style="display:none">Another reviewer pointed out that this was definitely an 80's book, as an employer who treated an employee this way would have made the girl very wealthy. <br />His treatment of her from the beginning was terrible. She was very naive. I was glad to see that she stood up to him for the majority of the book. There were some of her comments that I wanted to stand up and cheer. <br /><br />The end was too abrupt. I know this is JM's earlier writing, but I know that some of her newer offerings don't always give enough time at the end to show evidence of reconciliation. Other than a few sentences. It almost comes off as shallow. <br />'I'm sorry...I thought....Oh, you did...well your wrong..Oh, okay. Wedding.' <br />I am left wondering if the two have learned to communicate to avoid future 'big misunderstandings'. <br />If JM didn't do such a good job of providing the background to show where the H/H was predisposed to think as they did, I wouldn't insist on the 'closure' at the end. <br />When they (the writer) can completely sell you on the disfunction, as to why the characters can blow it so bad in their mistreatment of each other, they should be able to then show that the characters can now make healthy future decisions (HEA) and really deal with what caused the 'BIG misunderstanding'. <br />A wedding night does not a HEA prove after so much turmoil. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9459372006927775249" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_570347528" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/570347528" />
    <a title="Sophie ♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14918997-sophie"><img alt="Sophie ♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1374051209p2/14918997.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/570347528?book_show_action=true">Mar 25, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sophie ♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sophie ♥" href="/user/show/14918997-sophie">Sophie ♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14918997-sophie?shelf=my-reviews">my-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14918997-sophie?shelf=ebooks-i-own">ebooks-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14918997-sophie?shelf=romantic-suspense">romantic-suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14918997-sophie?shelf=setting-1900s">setting-1900s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14918997-sophie?shelf=read-2013">read-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14918997-sophie?shelf=contemp-romance">contemp-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer570347528" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17403949072453956922"><i>“He in­ter­rupted her with a boy­ish grin. "I promise I'll never wear your clothes, and I won't steal your al­lowances or your boyfriends ei­ther." Lau­ren couldn't help start­ing to smile as he fin­ished, "And if you swear never to call me Nicky again, I won't bite you."<br/>She stepped aside and let him in, then took his jacket and hung it in the closet. When she turned, Nick was lean­ing against the closed front door, his arms crossed over his chest. "On sec­ond thought," he grinned, "I take part </i></span>
  <span id="freeText17403949072453956922" style="display:none"><i>“He in­ter­rupted her with a boy­ish grin. "I promise I'll never wear your clothes, and I won't steal your al­lowances or your boyfriends ei­ther." Lau­ren couldn't help start­ing to smile as he fin­ished, "And if you swear never to call me Nicky again, I won't bite you."<br />She stepped aside and let him in, then took his jacket and hung it in the closet. When she turned, Nick was lean­ing against the closed front door, his arms crossed over his chest. "On sec­ond thought," he grinned, "I take part of that back. I'd love to bite you.”</i><br /><br />This book started out very slow for me. The first one third of this book seemed to just be the story of 'How Lauren Danner got everything a girl could possibly want' which didn't exactly provoke much empathy for her even when things started going wrong. Call it jealousy if you want, but I just thought Lauren was too perfect a heroine. She was confident, witty, stunningingly gorgeous and intelligent AND she got the man... I certainly didn't connect with her much.<br /><br />Another criticism I would have of this book is that it is the most abrupt book I've read. Although the beginning was a bit slow and not particularly interesting, things started happening out of nowhere. Like *bam* two days after meeting Lauren decides she's in love with Nick. Then *bam* they have sex. *Bam* Lauren's virginity goes out the window (and apparantly it doesn't even hurt). *Bam* he leaves her. *Bam* they get back together and now... they're getting married? I could go on but I'm sure you get the gist. There is a little bit of suspense at the end but its solved very quickly.<br /><br />Despite the book's shortcomings I did like the witty banter between the two and some of the things Lauren said to Nick were quite funny and I found myself reluctantly thinking "You go girl!" I'm sort of glad the book wrapped up quickly because I think I wouldn't have enjoyed reading more. I wouldn't say this book was the kind of quality you'd expect from Judith McNaught but then again I didn't read it with very high expectations. It was definitely better than Someone to Watch Over Me but it doesn't even begin to compare to Paradise and her historicals.<br /><br /><b>Rate: 3.5 - 4 stars</b> </span>
  <a data-text-id="17403949072453956922" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText3858214682929759921" style="display:none">This one totally follows the author's McNaughizing plots, with the hero eventually going into jerk mode over the big misunderstanding then having to come crawling back on his knees when he realizes how wrong he was.<br /><br />But c'mon, who doesnt like a man brought to his knees over his own actions?               <span id="reviewTextContainer361173762" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer3927193869948957451">This book was originally published in 1984. It was a hoot to read chick lit from more than 20 years ago:<br/><br/>* Lauren is a secretary with stenographic skills and uses a typewriter ... not a computer in sight!<br/>* Lauren wears velour shorts with a matching top ... I remember that fashion!<br/>* Lauren drives a six month old Trans Am.<br/>* Nick is an experienced 37-year-old; he's intense and carrying the hurt of the abandonment of his mother ... our typical hero from that time.<br/>* Lauren is a 23-year-old virgin (our</span>
  <span id="freeText3927193869948957451" style="display:none">This book was originally published in 1984. It was a hoot to read chick lit from more than 20 years ago:<br /><br />* Lauren is a secretary with stenographic skills and uses a typewriter ... not a computer in sight!<br />* Lauren wears velour shorts with a matching top ... I remember that fashion!<br />* Lauren drives a six month old Trans Am.<br />* Nick is an experienced 37-year-old; he's intense and carrying the hurt of the abandonment of his mother ... our typical hero from that time.<br />* Lauren is a 23-year-old virgin (our typical heroine from that time) who falls in love with Nick the second she meets him and gives herself to him within four days.<br />* Lauren is shocked when Nick doesn't want to marry after their experience together.<br />* Nick humiliates Lauren when he thinks he has discovered her betrayal and takes a month or so to discover the truth (he is, BTW, tortured by thoughts of her). He comes to her at her sick dad's house in a small town and wins her over (even though she yells at him to leave). They marry within three days. I bet there was a baby within the year cuz marriage and babies completed women back then.<br /><br />Back in the 80s, I read McNaught's books and enjoyed them. It was a simpler, more innocent time, I guess.<br /><br />I don't know if I could go back in time again anytime soon.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3927193869948957451" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_378370595" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/378370595" />
    <a title="Anita" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10765339-anita"><img alt="Anita" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1547669665p2/10765339.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/378370595?book_show_action=true">Sep 21, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anita" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anita" href="/user/show/10765339-anita">Anita</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/32414490-double-standards">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10765339-anita?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10765339-anita?shelf=kindle-la-city">kindle-la-city</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer378370595" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14415822166070570219">Judith McNaught is one of my favorite authors. I loved her historical-romance and well as her contemporary romances books. This one is an early one and it's not hard to believe this was published in 1984, it is very dated and doesn't stand the test of time very well at all. I haven't read a alpha, jerk hero like Nick in a long time, but if I remember my Judith McNaught history correctly, she had some doozies, but always redeemed them by the love of a good, solid, beautiful heroine. But, I do hav</span>
  <span id="freeText14415822166070570219" style="display:none">Judith McNaught is one of my favorite authors. I loved her historical-romance and well as her contemporary romances books. This one is an early one and it's not hard to believe this was published in 1984, it is very dated and doesn't stand the test of time very well at all. I haven't read a alpha, jerk hero like Nick in a long time, but if I remember my Judith McNaught history correctly, she had some doozies, but always redeemed them by the love of a good, solid, beautiful heroine. But, I do have to say that the writing is wonderful, far superior to a lot of what passes for contemporary romance these days. Angst and alpha A-Hole hero, Judith McNaught style, and I do mean style. Very few authors can make me swallow that combination, but JMN has such a flair and real style that I'm reading it and waiting to see what Lauren does to that Jerk, Nick. <br /><br />Lauren Danner's dad was downsized and then he had a massive heart attack leaving his family swimming in debt. He contacts a rich, distant relative and asks him to give Lauren a job. With a love of piano and a music degree, that and $1.00 will buy you a cup of coffee. Lauren heads to Detroit and, hopefully, a job that can help dig her family out of debt. What she finds there is a smarmy, nasty relative who wants her to commit industrial espionage for him. Lauren wants no part of that, but fate has different ideas.<br /><br />Nick Sinclair is a handsome, arrogant and the extremely wealthy president of Global Industries. He is tough in business and always in control with the women in his life. When he rescues Lauren he is struck by her beauty and wit. Against his will he is drawn to her and sets out to win her over, all on his terms, of course.<br /><br />Lauren is half in love after their first encounter and is all in after their weekend together. Then the omissions, by both of them, loom large and when Lauren discovers Nick's tragic childhood, her secret makes her hope for an HEA seem really, really dim.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14415822166070570219" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/628308398" />
    <a title="ElaineY" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1301782-elainey"><img alt="ElaineY" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1478668491p2/1301782.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/628308398?book_show_action=true">May 30, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="ElaineY" class="user" itemprop="url" name="ElaineY" href="/user/show/1301782-elainey">ElaineY</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9780671614553" href="/book/show/4011440-double-standards">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1301782-elainey?shelf=romance-contemporary">romance-contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1301782-elainey?shelf=5-star-books">5-star-books</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer628308398" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3144972582982514982"><b>REVIEW OF AUDIOBOOK; FEB 22, 2014<br/>Narrator: Margaret Ball</b><br/><br/>I love these oldies. Even when I know it'll be like a train wreck approaching and I still can't look the other way.<br/><br/>And so it was with DS, written in 1986. The good thing about it, when I am brave enough to tackle a romance written in the bad ol '80s is that I can't complain about any nasty surprises. I am prepared for the nasty and all that I judge the book on is whether the story's compelling and whether I find the male lead attractive (or</span>
  <span id="freeText3144972582982514982" style="display:none"><b>REVIEW OF AUDIOBOOK; FEB 22, 2014<br />Narrator: Margaret Ball</b><br /><br />I love these oldies. Even when I know it'll be like a train wreck approaching and I still can't look the other way.<br /><br />And so it was with DS, written in 1986. The good thing about it, when I am brave enough to tackle a romance written in the bad ol '80s is that I can't complain about any nasty surprises. I am prepared for the nasty and all that I judge the book on is whether the story's compelling and whether I find the male lead attractive (or can forgive him by the end of the book).<br /><br />Double Standards is quintessential 80s contemporary romance and I loved it. Lauren isn't just a virgin, she's smart, with a great sense of humor and able to hold her own against the successful, wealthy Nick Sinclair.<br /><br />It's been thirty years since I first read this and, as is to be expected, had forgotten the details. I did still remember, though, that it had to do with the heroine infiltrating the hero's company and the train wreck that follows when they fall in love. I'd normally stay away from these nowadays but nothing in my audiobook shelves interested me, I was already bored with J D Robb (stopped at Vengeance, book 6) and decided on this old McNaught when a friend offered. I borrowed two from her - the other one is <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/353938.Someone_to_Watch_Over_Me?ac=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Someone to Watch Over Her</a> whereas DB was originally from my friend's cassette tapes she made in CDs first, them mp3. I'm hoping this and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/129617.Perfect" rel="nofollow noopener">Perfect</a> will be re-released. There are so many good romances and romantic suspenses out there from yesteryear that I want to see in downloadable mp3 with new narrators.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3144972582982514982" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText514847129928405018" style="display:none">Double Standard - NR<br />McNaught, Judith<br /><br />In the exclusive, glittering world of business superstars, Nick Sinlair was a legend...<br /><br />The ruggedly handsome president of Global Industries handled his business the way he handled his women-with charm, daring, and ruthless self-control. A man used to the very best, Nick hired Laura Danner, and assumed that the proud beauty would soon be another easy conquest. But Laura's flashing wit and rare spirit dazzle him-and slowly, against his will, he was intrigued, challenged-and in love.<br /><br />Yet Laura was living a lie, a charade that became more dangerous with every passing moment. Trapped in a web of deceit, she fought her growing love for Nick. Her secret could destroy his fragile trust-and the promise of life with the most compelling man she had ever met!<br /><br />I usually like McNaught's books, but this one just didn't do it for me at all. The female protagonist was just too innocent and naive for my taste.</span>

<div id="review_1208277738" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1208277738" />
    <a title="Chanel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33551441-chanel"><img alt="Chanel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580169084p2/33551441.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1208277738?book_show_action=true">Feb 22, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chanel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chanel" href="/user/show/33551441-chanel">Chanel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/33551441-chanel?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1208277738" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8878689811231025857">Sometimes you just need an oldie but a goodie. I debated whether to reread a different McNaught book instead of this one but I'm part of a reading challenge and there's not a lot of January left so I chose this one instead. Let me tell you, I'm so glad I did! You ever remember a book but not quite remember it all at the same time? This was that book for me. Talk about an emotional rollercoaster. I wasn't ready.<br/><br/>The premise is simple. Philip Whitworth suspects he has a spy in his ranks because eve</span>
  <span id="freeText8878689811231025857" style="display:none">Sometimes you just need an oldie but a goodie. I debated whether to reread a different McNaught book instead of this one but I'm part of a reading challenge and there's not a lot of January left so I chose this one instead. Let me tell you, I'm so glad I did! You ever remember a book but not quite remember it all at the same time? This was that book for me. Talk about an emotional rollercoaster. I wasn't ready.<br /><br />The premise is simple. Philip Whitworth suspects he has a spy in his ranks because every time he bids on a contract, his competition, Sinco, always beats him out. He has narrowed it down to the six people who are privy to the information and decides he wants to send a spy inside Sinco's business to ferret them out. Enter Lauren Danner. She's come to interview for a job courtesy of her ailing father because her family is falling deeper into debt and they need the money. The Whitworths are like seventh generation distant cousins so Philip was doing her a favor. When she hears what he's offering, at first she agrees but the more she thinks about it, the more it didn't sit well and ultimately she fails her interview on purpose in order to not get the job.<br /><br />What she didn't count on was meeting Nick Sinclair and falling for him literally and figuratively. From here on out, the rest of the story is an up and down emotional rollercoaster. Lauren is very intelligent if sexually naive and Nick is very attuned to Lauren but tries very hard to keep emotionally distant. It's a constant battle of wills while trying to stay true to themselves. I can't go into much more detail without spoiling but for a book that was written before I was even born, it never fails to impress me every time I read it. I cried a lot and it wasn't always sad tears! I can just put myself in both of their shoes and feel what they're feeling at each time. It's no secret that I adore Judith McNaught and I'm definitely glad to be given an excuse to re-read any of her works at any time.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8878689811231025857" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1089879144" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1089879144" />
    <a title="Tracy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15686622-tracy"><img alt="Tracy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1419741819p2/15686622.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1089879144?book_show_action=true">Oct 26, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tracy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tracy" href="/user/show/15686622-tracy">Tracy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1089879144" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5655627484730623077">This is 4 ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️ for me. <br/>I don't know whether to laugh or cry when I finish a book by Judith McNaught. I really love her writing and she is by far one of my favourite authors. <br/>My problem is that when I start one of her books u find it hard to put down and I usually stay up until the wee hours of the night. I pay the price dearly the next day. I can't wait to read her books and then I am sad when I finish one because it means there are fewer left I her collection for me to devour - so I try and</span>
  <span id="freeText5655627484730623077" style="display:none">This is 4 ⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️ for me. <br />I don't know whether to laugh or cry when I finish a book by Judith McNaught. I really love her writing and she is by far one of my favourite authors. <br />My problem is that when I start one of her books u find it hard to put down and I usually stay up until the wee hours of the night. I pay the price dearly the next day. I can't wait to read her books and then I am sad when I finish one because it means there are fewer left I her collection for me to devour - so I try and savour them by only reading one every few months. <br />While I have liked some of her other books more than this one I really loved the characters and the sub characters too. <br />Nick is handsome and powerful and as always just a little damaged so he had depth of character. He has a tender side which he hides away and rarely comes out - except with Lauren. She is strong and smart and beautiful and has depth as well. The chemistry between these main characters was excellent and I cheered them on. <br />A few things that I didn't love - the ending, like the last couple books I have read of hers was a bit too abrupt. It is as though the author pours all her heart and soul into the story but then doesn't have the energy to draw out the ending. I need just a bit more. I wanted a glimpse of the characters more than right after the big ending. There also seemed to be a couple things that seemed like loose ends. Phillip claimed there was a spy who was just slightly undercutting his buds but there is never a reason explained for that. The lack of background check on Lauren until the security company investigated was surprising to me. But ultimately it felt like things were nicely tied up in the end (though abrupt). Can't wait to read her next book on my list!</span>
  <a data-text-id="5655627484730623077" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7111812387790958014">The story of Lauren, a naive young woman trying to help her family out of debt, and Nick, a handsome and wealthy company president whom she falls for.<br/><br/>Nick is enchanted by Lauren when they first meet and pursues her until she gives in to his charms, but although Lauren falls head over heels for him, a weekend is all he wants with her, breaking her heart.<br/><br/>She uses that experience to grow a backbone and doesn't let the handsome jerk walk all over her, which gives her plenty of cookie points. At the </span>
  <span id="freeText7111812387790958014" style="display:none">The story of Lauren, a naive young woman trying to help her family out of debt, and Nick, a handsome and wealthy company president whom she falls for.<br /><br />Nick is enchanted by Lauren when they first meet and pursues her until she gives in to his charms, but although Lauren falls head over heels for him, a weekend is all he wants with her, breaking her heart.<br /><br />She uses that experience to grow a backbone and doesn't let the handsome jerk walk all over her, which gives her plenty of cookie points. At the same time her attitude keeps Nick out of balance and forces him to face the issues of his past that keep him from reaching for happiness<br /><br />Enjoyable, if dated, story with one of my favorite tropes, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[a hero grovelling after he messes up, although there wasn't nearly as much grovelling as I would have liked <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, and a happy ending.</span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('gmlq+TPWcFHNVziSMZk81z+rabmMwKSA4lwjV0XXMS3dvx/W1PhhkQecvM7tcH6WSYHeEkeGEeXlGF98mK0bdA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ytUiQubyGe8yOTP37Ju3sq+k7LUkPFHiTowSrg2M3HSVA1dtAdwIL/jyt6swcvXz2Y5bHu965IdJyG6F0Pb2LQ==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>
